## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening. Classical constitutive models combine strain hardening with temperature-dependent softening factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (basic plastic strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Hollomon equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (exponential saturation hardening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal factor)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with Arrhenius thermal softening)
- Swift law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with offset strain)
- Swift with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (Swift law with temperature dependence)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**c3 (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T) (polynomial hardening with linear thermal factor)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (1/T))) (thermally activated deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → stress = f(strain) * g(T), where g(T) is a decreasing function of temperature
- Elastic modulus temperature dependence → Young's modulus often varies linearly or quadratically with T: E(T) = c0 - c1*T
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicates stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Power-law hardening exponent → epsilon**c with c typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals in plastic regime
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c0 / T) or exp(-c0 * T) terms reflect thermally activated dislocation mechanisms
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress represents initial yield strength before hardening
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (T - c0) or (1 - c0*T) reflecting melting-point-normalized temperature
- Combined additive-multiplicative structure → (yield + hardening) * (thermal softening) * (rate sensitivity) is the canonical Johnson-Cook decomposition
